praise for his willingness to play on despite major injuries, with manager Solskjær saying he would "run through a brick wall for you",<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> while his captain <a href="/wiki/Harry_Maguire" title="Harry Maguire">Harry Maguire</a> describes him as a battler.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Louis_van_Gaal" title="Louis van Gaal">Louis van Gaal</a>, Rashford's first senior manager, and Fletcher Moss coach Dave Horrocks have both praised his ability to handle criticism, with van Gaal saying it was amongst his best assets.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He is seen as a similar type of player to <a href="/wiki/Thierry_Henry" title="Thierry Henry">Thierry Henry</a> in terms of style of play, physical attributes and end product.<sup id="cite_ref-Rash365_194-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rash365-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> Van Gaal said his performances at a young age were similar to those of <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Kluivert" title="Patrick Kluivert">Patrick Kluivert</a>, who he had managed at <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax</a> in the 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> Growing up, the player he most tried to emulate was Brazilian striker <a href="/wiki/Ronaldo_(Brazilian_footballer)" title="Ronaldo (Brazilian footballer)">Ronaldo</a>, having watched him score a <a href="/wiki/Hat-trick_(association_football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hat-trick (association football)">hat-trick</a> for <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF" title="Real Madrid CF">Real Madrid</a> in a <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_UEFA_Champions_League_knockout_stage#Second_leg" title="2002–03 UEFA Champions League knockout stage">Champions League quarter-final</a> in the first match he attended live at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Idol_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Idol-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> Speaking about Ronaldo, Rashford said: "I've grown up watching so much of him and his games. He always played free, and went out there and expressed himself. When you do that, that's when you play your best football."<sup id="cite_ref-Idol_230-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Idol-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> Rashford said that Cristiano Ronaldo and <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Rooney" title="Wayne Rooney">Wayne Rooney</a> were United players he idolised in his youth, having seen them join the team at an early age and watched many of their games live,<sup id="cite_ref-FFTInt_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FFTInt-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> and said of Ronaldo that "there is no bigger inspiration in football" after Rashford had begun his own professional career;<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> comparisons have been made between the development of the two by Southgate, Solskjær, and McGuinness.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBCMaking_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCMaking-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> He credits Rooney's professionalism with helping him mature in the early stages of career, describing how he was "always ready to play and give his best",<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> and has been tipped by Little to break Rooney's <a href="/wiki/List_of_Manchester_United_F.C._records_and_statistics#Goalscorers" title="List of Manchester United F.C. records and statistics">goalscoring record</a> of 253 goals for the club.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> He has been described as a "student of the game", continuing to watch matches of players such as <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Messi" title="Lionel Messi">Lionel Messi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Ag%C3%BCero" title="Sergio Agüero">Sergio Agüero</a> with the idea of studying and learning to improve his own game.<sup id="cite_ref-FFTMWMH_19-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FFTMWMH-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Charity_and_activism">Charity and activism</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_poverty_campaign">Food poverty campaign</span></h3>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:30%; ;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1012376600"/>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"It is not beyond the bounds of possibility that a <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> striker's name will be sung on <a href="/wiki/Anfield" title="Anfield">the Kop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Goodison_Park" title="Goodison Park">the Gwladys Street</a>. He has the sort of principles and moral values that most people hold. He's clever, passionate and well advised".</div>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">—<a href="/wiki/Ian_Byrne_(politician)" title="Ian Byrne (politician)">Ian Byrne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament_(United_Kingdom)" title="Member of Parliament (United Kingdom)">MP</a> and co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Fans_Supporting_Foodbanks" title="Fans Supporting Foodbanks">Fans Supporting Foodbanks</a> praising Rashford's activism.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>In October 2019, Rashford set up the <i>In the Box</i> campaign with <a href="/wiki/Selfridges" title="Selfridges">Selfridges</a> to give homeless people essential items over the Christmas period,<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RashPF_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RashPF-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> something he had wanted to do when first training with United as a youth.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> He and his mother visited homeless shelters to personally hand the boxes out, while also sending some to a children's home in his grandmother's home country of <a href="/wiki/St_Kitts_and_Nevis" class="mw-redirect" title="St Kitts and Nevis">St Kitts and Nevis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RashCharity_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RashCharity-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> He was reportedly frustrated by the limited outreach the campaign resulted in.<sup id="cite_ref-RashfordSuperhero_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RashfordSuperhero-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2020, during the UK lockdown imposed by <a href="/wiki/Second_Johnson_ministry" title="Second Johnson ministry">Boris Johnson's government</a> in response to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="COVID-19 pandemic in the United Kingdom">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, Rashford teamed up with the poverty and <a href="/wiki/Food_waste" title="Food waste">food waste</a> charity <a href="/wiki/FareShare" title="FareShare">FareShare</a> to deliver meals to those in the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester" title="Greater Manchester">Greater Manchester</a> area who were no longer receiving their <a href="/wiki/School_meal#United_Kingdom" title="School meal">free school meals</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> as well as to children who attended <a href="/wiki/Community_centre" title="Community centre">community centres</a> and <a href="/wiki/School_breakfast_club" title="School breakfast club">school breakfast clubs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> Rashford initially contacted FareShare to make a "substantial" donation, but after discussion with CEO Lindsay Boswell, he decided to provide his full support.<sup id="cite_ref-RashfordSuperhero_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RashfordSuperhero-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> With an initial target of supporting 400,000 children in the region, the initiative quickly raised over £20&#160;million to provide food for children nationwide who, if still at school, would be receiving free school meals.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RashCharity_242-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RashCharity-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> On 11 June, Rashford revealed that the charity had been able to reach three million children across the country,<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> a figure which rose to four million the following month.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 15 June, Rashford wrote an <a href="/wiki/Open_letter" title="Open letter">open letter</a> to the UK government calling on them to end UK <a href="/wiki/Child_poverty" title="Child poverty">child poverty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> A day later, the government announced a change in policy regarding the extension of free school meals for children during the summer holidays,<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> with Rashford's campaign credited as a major turning point in governmental talks;<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> Rashford described himself as "proud" of what he had helped accomplish on behalf of 1.3&#160;million children.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> His actions were described as a "political masterclass" by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> and was praised for countering comments made by <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Health_and_Social_Care" title="Secretary of State for Health and Social Care">Secretary of State for Health and Social Care</a> <a href="/wiki/Matt_Hancock" title="Matt Hancock">Matt Hancock</a> regarding the contributions of footballers.<sup id="cite_ref-RashfordSuperhero_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RashfordSuperhero-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup> On 1 September, in an attempt to tackle child food poverty, Rashford announced that he had set up the <i>Child Food Poverty Task Force</i> in collaboration with several UK food shops, manufacturers, charities, and delivery companies.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> Later that month, he said he was "disappointed by the lack of empathy" being shown by <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a> members of parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After he was appointed <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of the Order of the British Empire">Member of the Order of the British Empire</a> (MBE) in October, Rashford vowed to continue his campaign,<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> and a week later he began a petition on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Parliament_petitions_website" title="UK Parliament petitions website">UK Parliament petitions website</a> to end child food poverty, with demands made for expansion of the free school meals program, provision of meals and activities during school holidays, and an increase in value of Healthy Start vouchers.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> The petition received over 100,000 signatures in 10 hours, meaning it had passed the threshold to be considered for parliamentary debate, and received over 200,000 signatures in the first day.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> With the petition close to 300,000 signatures after less than a week, <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> proposed an <a href="/wiki/Opposition_day" title="Opposition day">opposition day</a> debate on the matter of extending free school meals,<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> which was rejected by a majority of 61.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> Rashford criticised those who voted against it as lacking humanity.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Later that week, Rashford began using his <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> account to promote cafés, individual people and local business offering assistance to FareShare to help the impoverished around the country.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> He received the local backing of the <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Greater_Manchester" title="Mayor of Greater Manchester">Mayor of Greater Manchester</a> <a href="/wiki/Andy_Burnham" title="Andy Burnham">Andy Burnham</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Co-operative_Group" title="The Co-operative Group">The Co-operative Group</a>, to provide 1,000 food vouchers over half-term,<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> which was quickly followed by councils and businesses across the North-West backing the efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> He described himself as "blown away" by the nationwide support which followed,<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> with over 100 businesses, charities, and local councils quickly pledging to the campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> The same day, FareShare announced their new warehouse would be named <i>Melanie Maynard House</i> in honour of Rashford's mother,<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> and it was revealed they had received donations in record numbers in the day following the Parliamentary debate.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> In the following days, over 1,200 had signed up to provide free meals over the half-term,<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup> and Rashford's petition became only the sixth to reach <a href="/wiki/UK_Parliament_petitions_website#Petitions_with_more_than_a_million_signatures" title="UK Parliament petitions website">over one million signatures</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> On 8 November, it was announced that, because of Rashford's campaign, the government would be providing funding of almost £400m over the next 12 months to support the cost of food and household bills to poor families.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> At the end of the month, former Manchester United manager <a href="/wiki/Alex_Ferguson" title="Alex Ferguson">Alex Ferguson</a> and venture capitalist <a href="/wiki/Michael_Moritz" title="Michael Moritz">Michael Moritz</a> pledged to double any donations through a Christmas fundraising appeal set up by Rashford in conjunction with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> newspaper, with Ferguson declaring himself "proud" of Rashford.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> The campaign had raised over £2.7 million by the beginning of January.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2021, Rashford again used his Twitter account to begin highlighting the "unacceptable" food packages parents had received through supplier Chartwells, an offspring of <a href="/wiki/Compass_Group" title="Compass Group">Compass Group</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Boris_Johnson" title="Boris Johnson">Johnson</a> again pressured into conducting a review into the situation after the pair had a conversation regarding the matter;<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup> during a <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister%27s_Questions" title="Prime Minister&#39;s Questions">Prime Minister's Questions</a> on 13 January, Johnson credited Rashford as being more effective opposition than the actual <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Opposition_(United_Kingdom)" title="Leader of the Opposition (United Kingdom)">Leader of the Opposition</a> <a href="/wiki/Keir_Starmer" title="Keir Starmer">Keir Starmer</a>, the current <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Leader of the Labour Party (UK)">Leader of the Labour Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Universal_Credit_campaigning">Universal Credit campaigning</span></h4>
<p>In October 2020, Rashford publicly questioned <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_the_Exchequer" title="Chancellor of the Exchequer">Chancellor of the Exchequer</a> <a href="/wiki/Rishi_Sunak" title="Rishi Sunak">Rishi Sunak</a> regarding a permanent £20 increase in <a href="/wiki/Universal_Credit" title="Universal Credit">Universal Credit</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup> stressing his concern that many families would be "counting down the days" until the scheduled reversal the following April.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup> A member of Rashford's team told <i>The Times</i> the permanent annual increase of £1,040 was the "missing piece" in their campaign strategy.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> At the end of December, it was revealed by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> that Rashford would have discussions with <a href="/wiki/Th%C3%A9r%C3%A8se_Coffey" title="Thérèse Coffey">Thérèse Coffey</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Work_and_Pensions" title="Secretary of State for Work and Pensions">Secretary of State for Work and Pensions</a>, regarding the permanent increase in Universal Credit;<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup> Rashford had previously been critical of Coffey during the initial stages of his campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Recognition">Recognition</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rashford_Mural.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/85/Rashford_Mural.jpg/220px-Rashford_Mural.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/85/Rashford_Mural.jpg/330px-Rashford_Mural.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/85/Rashford_Mural.jpg/440px-Rashford_Mural.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4160" data-file-height="3120" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rashford_Mural.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mural of Marcus Rashford in <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:30%; ;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1012376600"/>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"I have known him since being a kid of 7 years of age, and seen him develop through the ranks of Manchester United into a truly wonderful person. Apart from his football life, what he has achieved in the last few months is quite astonishing, how he has helped the people in need is a truly amazing achievement. I would like to congratulate him on that. He has shown to young people in particular there is a different way of dealing with life. He has shown great humility, he has shown courage to do what he did".</div>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">—<a href="/wiki/Alex_Ferguson" title="Alex Ferguson">Alex Ferguson</a>, former <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> manager, praising Rashford's activism.<sup id="cite_ref-FWATribute_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FWATribute-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>In the wake of the popularity generated by his charity work, Rashford signed with American rapper <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>'s entertainment agency <a href="/wiki/Roc_Nation" title="Roc Nation">Roc Nation</a> in April 2020, with president Michael Yormark saying he was a "shining example" of somebody who was "passionate about community".<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup> On 15 July, he received an honorary doctorate from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Manchester" title="University of Manchester">University of Manchester</a> in recognition of his work to end child poverty in the UK, becoming the youngest person to receive an honorary doctorate from the university.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> His efforts also led to him being featured on the September cover of <a href="/wiki/British_Vogue" title="British Vogue">British <i>Vogue</i></a><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> "Activism Now" edition alongside <a href="/wiki/Adwoa_Aboah" title="Adwoa Aboah">Adwoa Aboah</a>, which he downplayed, saying that he "had a voice and a platform that could be used to at least ask the questions".<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup> In October, Rashford was appointed MBE in the <a href="/wiki/2020_Birthday_Honours" title="2020 Birthday Honours">2020 Birthday Honours</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup> and was also a recipient of the <i>City of Manchester Award</i> for his "outstanding and exceptional contribution to the city".<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/Pride_of_Britain_Awards#2020" title="Pride of Britain Awards">2020 Pride of Britain Awards</a>, he won the award for <i>Special Recognition</i> for his campaign against child food poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup> Local <a href="/wiki/Street_art" title="Street art">street artist</a> Akse honoured Rashford with a mural of him in <a href="/wiki/Withington" title="Withington">Withington</a>, a suburb of Manchester where Rashford lived at the time he signed for Fletcher Moss Rangers.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Voice_(British_newspaper)" title="The Voice (British newspaper)">The Voice</a>, the only <a href="/wiki/British_African-Caribbean_people" title="British African-Caribbean people">British African-Caribbean</a> newspaper in the United Kingdom, named Rashford on the <i>Football Black List</i>, an initiative designed to celebrate influential black people in football.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup> Rashford was named as <i>Campaigner Of The Year</i> in the 2020 <a href="/wiki/GQ" title="GQ">GQ</a> Men Of The Year awards.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> Although not on the main category shortlist, he was the recipient of a special award at the <i><a href="/wiki/BBC_Sports_Personality_of_the_Year_Award" title="BBC Sports Personality of the Year Award">BBC Sports Personality of the Year Award</a>'s</i>, with a documentary airing the following night.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup> At the annual <i><a href="/wiki/The_Best_FIFA_Football_Awards_2020" title="The Best FIFA Football Awards 2020">The Best FIFA Football Awards 2020</a></i> held in December, Rashford was the inaugural winner of the <i>FIFA Foundation Award</i>, with the FIFA Foundation CEO <a href="/wiki/Youri_Djorkaeff" title="Youri Djorkaeff">Youri Djorkaeff</a> also donating £75,000 to the charities.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup> In November 2020, Rashford was recognised for his sporting achievements and his activism, by being included in the <a href="/wiki/Powerlist_2020" title="Powerlist 2020">2020</a> edition of the annual <i><a href="/wiki/Powerlist" title="Powerlist">Powerlist</a></i> of the 100 most influential Black Britons. <sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2021, Rashford was awarded the <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian_Footballer_of_the_Year" title="The Guardian Footballer of the Year">The Guardian Footballer of the Year</a></i>, an award given to "a player who has done something remarkable, whether by overcoming adversity, helping others or setting a sporting example by acting with exceptional honesty",<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup> and was the recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Football_Writers%27_Association" title="Football Writers&#39; Association">Football Writers' Association</a>'s (FWA) <i><a href="/wiki/FWA_Tribute_Award" title="FWA Tribute Award">Tribute Award</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FWATribute_289-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FWATribute-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup> In February, he was listed on <a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a> magazine's <a href="/wiki/Time_100#Time_100_Next_list" title="Time 100">100 Next list</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup> selected as an "advocate".<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literacy_campaign">Literacy campaign</span></h3>
<p>For the 2020 <a href="/wiki/World_Book_Day" title="World Book Day">World Book Day</a>, Rashford was one of a number of celebrities who supported a campaign to help share a million stories.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup> He also agreed to judge a poetry competition for children with hearing impairments, and began learning <a href="/wiki/Sign_language" title="Sign language">sign language</a> in preparation.<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RashPF_240-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RashPF-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November, he teamed with <a href="/wiki/Macmillan_Publishers" title="Macmillan Publishers">Macmillan Publishers</a> to launch a <a href="/wiki/Book_discussion_club" title="Book discussion club">book club</a> to help vulnerable and underprivileged children experience the "escapism of reading",<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup> with Rashford saying that reading shouldn't be something a family should have to budget for.<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup> Under the partnership, Rashford announced he would be releasing a children's motivational book titled "<i>You Are A Champion</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
